< text>
This is the only park I've found in the neighborhood where my daughter and grandson reside. The park is always clean. However, I haven't found public bathrooms and the park looks to be new, or at least they haven't planted many trees here. Not much for shade so it can get pretty uncomfortable in the summer. But the children seem to love the playground a lot. Usually lots of children. If you have a single child who comes alone they will most likely have other child (ren) to play with soon after he/she arrives.</text>

<Rate>1<//Rate><review>My wife and I hired FETCH PET CARE of Los Angeles Westside to arrange for a petsitter to stay in our home and watch over our beloved animal companions while we're out of town. We were impressed by their reviews on Google and Yelp. Their website claims "Fetch Pet Care's experienced sitters are background checked, bonded, and insured pet lovers." They quickly set us up with their sitter/walker named Anthony (Tony) Vercillo who outwardly seemed like a good candidate to take good care of our dog & cat. So, we agreed to book him for the 10 days we'd be away.

In the late morning of day 7, our cleaning crew came in for a routine sprucing and they were so shocked by the ill state of the apartment they felt compelled to contact us. They texted me photos of feces and urine left in various rooms, beer cans & liquor bottles filled our recycling bin, piles of garbage spilling onto the floor and other examples of disarray uncharacteristic to us and our pets. They also told us that a woman was in the apartment with the sitter (although that had not been permitted by us), and another dog that didn't belong to us.

Alarmed by the situation but thinking it can still be handled rather easily, I called Fetch Pet Care to have them address the situation.  They told me they would replace the current pet sitter with a more responsible person as quickly and uneventfully as possible. What I didn't know was that the representative from Fetch Pet Care would soon make an irreversible management error that would threaten the security of our dog, cat and home.

The Fetch representative called the sitter first to confront him about the situation over the phone, while he still had our dog with him. We found out later that this confrontation then led the sitter to openly put the blame on the woman who was with him and that the woman quickly became unhinged as a result. They argued and then she suddenly disappeared with our sweet, sensitive dog.

We were scared out of our minds, though, not knowing what was going on with our poor dog but we couldn't do much else but wait. At some point, we were eventually told that the kidnapper was a diagnosed schizophrenic and possibly more unstable than we'd initially imagined. We were worried sick about any possible misstep that could cause a big reaction from this woman. We kept calling the police, the park rangers, the Fetch representative and even the sitter for updates but for many hours none came. A couple hours later, the woman contacted the sitter again and this time she demanded ransom money from him in exchange for our dog's safe return.

Late in the evening, our dog was finally turned over to a representative of Fetch Pet Care.  We cut our trip short and returned the very next day.  Upon our return we took our dog to the vet for a checkup and though her general heath was okay, she had lost 4lbs in during those 7 days and was slightly anemic.  Our cat also looked as if he hadn't been fed in several days but other than that he was fine. Our home was mostly restored by a thorough cleaning. So we're okay. But we're not okay. This never should happen to anyone.

Fetch refunded our money and paid for the additional expenses we incurred as a result of this ordeal. While we are trying to be accepting of this gesture, it doesn't come close to repaying us for this horror of a day that never would have happened if only they had managed their human resources issue in a more sensible, secure way. Nor would any of this happened if they had properly vetted this sitter before touting him to all of their clients as an appropriate caregiver. I seriously question every decent review for this company and warn everyone to stay far away from the caregiver named Anthony (Tony) Vercillo. He will trash your home, fail to feed your pets, fail to walk your dog regularly, fail to clean the litter box, and expose your furry loved ones to a dognapper.<//review>< pics>

<Rate>5</Rate>< Text>
I spent two weeks in Japan in summer of 2013 and was looking for an LA sushi and seafood restaurant that could replicate what I had there. I tried many places before I found Musha, which is the closest I think you can come to that experience without an 11-hour flight.

Everything in Musha, from the menus to the seating arrangements (expect to take off your shoes before you go into the dining room) are traditional. The selection is short of sushi and favors more the small-portions plates commonly found in Japan.

All in all, it's the place to go to if you want a little slice of real Japan right here in Los Angeles.</Text>

<Text>Quickie:
+ Intimate joint with a cool spin on Japanese cuisine
+ OMG the rissoto

---

Place:
Musha is definitely one of my most favorite restaurants in the Torrance area - I've went numerous times and have always left quite "ureshii." The place is on the cozier side but by no means inconveniently small... you can sit at the sushi bar, the booths and tables against the wall or the big family style table in the middle.

Food:
The food options are plentiful - I have had the Cheese Risotto and it's superbly delicious (doesn't hurt that it actually comes served in a whole wheel of cheese). I've tried the variations of sushi and desserts as have my friends and never has there been a poor review. Prices are pretty ordinary - nothing that will break the bank which is nice. Be daring and try anything - you won't be disappointed, I'm sure.

Overall:
It's not pajamas-and-house-shoes casual but you don't have to dress to the nines either - I love it. Need a nice restaurant to show off to out-of-town friends? Then, Musha is the place for you.<//Text>< rating>

<user_id>114629017963490151120</user_id><username>Esther Kim<//username><Time>1451624913744<//Time>< rate>
4</rate>
< text>
I came here with Gardenia H. and KW for a birthday dinner earlier this year. The restaurant is located in a large plaza so parking is plentiful. We got lucky and found a spot right in front of the restaurant. We had a reservation so we were quickly seated.

We shared the following:
-- TUNA POKE: Hawaiian style sashimi diced ahi tuna marinated with seaweed, garlic, sesame oil, citrus, wasabi, and soy sauce served with rice crackers
I do not eat raw fish, so I did not partake of this dish. Both Gardenia and KW liked it.
-- MUSHA'S FRIED CHICKEN: Chicken marinated with sake, soy sauce, ginger, and garlic. Served with spicy grated daikon and ponzu sauce.
This did not look like what I thought it would look like. It looked more like chicken cutlet. The ponzu sauce was good but overall this dish was just okay. I wish they would rename this dish so people would have more realistic expectations (look at the picture. That is not what normal fried chicken looks like)
-- UDON VONGOLE: Asari (manilla clams) and assorted mushrooms sauteed with garlic, butter, sake and soy sauce. One of our East meets West dishes.
I have to say, based on the appearance I did not think I would care for this dish very much. So I was pleasantly surprised that I liked it. One complaint however is that the garlic flavour was very subtle (I love garlic and was hoping for a stronger flavour in this dish).
-- EBI MAYO MAYO: Spicy mayo glazed shrimp. Bite-size fried shrimp glazed with Musha's original sweet & spicy mayo sauce. With a texture and taste that will make you say "ahh~"
This was similar to the honey walnut shrimp you can get at Chinese restaurants. I really liked this dish--I love shrimp and it was prepared to be quite delicious here. It was served on a bed of salad, which I appreciated in this case because it helped offset all the mayo. Probably my favourite dish of the night.
-- MUSHA'S CHEESE RISOTTO: Italian dish with Japanese creation. Japanese grain brown rice cooked with chicken broth. Then panfried with bacon, onion, and a touch of heavy cream. Served in a whole cheese bowl to your table.
It is pretty cool that they bring out the risotto in a block of cheese, although it would have been even cooler if that is how they served it to us (the server scoops it into a bowl for the table). It was interesting since it was not the typical risotto rice used; it was also not as soft as I would like, but it was still good. However, would I get it again? Probably not.
-- BLACK SESAME ICE CREAM WITH BLACK HONEY AND SOY POWDER
This was a very interesting flavour. There was a crunchy topping which was nice... I'm glad we tried this out but I would probably not get it again.
-- CREAM BRULEE
I am not sure if the menu calling it "cream brulee" is a typo or not, because the dessert is very creamy so perhaps they were trying to be clever? I always love watching servers torch creme brulee at the table; creme brulee is my favourite dessert and I enjoyed it here. Always a wonderful way to end a meal.

Overall we enjoyed most of the food here and had a great time with good company. If you are in the area and the food I described sounds appealing, stop on by!</text>

<time>1409361909174</time><Rating>2< /Rating>< review>
Came here on a Saturday night when they first opened at 6. Apparently all the couple tables were reserved so my friend and I had to sit next to each other at the big communal table. We both wanted to get dinner before a movie nearby and I came here based off all the great yelp reviews. I was definitely disappointed.

We ordered:
the beef/potato croquette to start, followed by the fried chicken, beef tenderloin, and yaki onigiri.

The croquette was a special. It was really crispy on the outside and soft on the inside and lacked flavor. The clash of textures was a bit jarring and the overall dish was very disappointing.

The fried chicken was good. Not great, but just your standard fried chicken I guess. I felt pretty neutral about it - once again, I could have gone with more flavor.

The beef tenderloin is the only thing I would order again, although it was comparatively on the pricier side ($15).  It was well seasoned and cooked quickly on the grill to our liking - so I could only blame myself if I messed that up! The side sauce complimented it well.

The yaki onigiri is just what it sounds like - crispy fried brown rice without embellishments which worked well with the beef.

The meal ended with some complimentary tea.

Overall, the food was pretty bland and unimpressive. I will not be returning.</review>

< Text>
Yet another solid recommendation from the ex-wife, Hanae K. She raved and raved about the cheese risotto that comes in a block of cheese. Of course I had to try check this out.

Other than the cheese risotto, we ordered the buta kakuni, the jidori chicken in yuzu sauce, ribeye skewers and the portabello mushroom with truffle oil. My favorite dish of the night were the mushrooms. We got to grill them on the table on a cute little charcoal grill and dipped them piping hot in the truffle oil.

The buta kakuni is very moist and tender. The jidori chicken is pretty good but I mostly only liked the crispy chicken skin. As for the risotto, they use a different rice that has a more substantial texture. It was delicious but the dish was quite heavy.

The ambiance is pretty casual. In fact, my sister, her bf, my bf, and I shared a large table in the center of the restaurant with several other parties. Luckily we got a corner seat so it wasn't too hard to have a conversation.

The service is pretty good but the food did take a while to come out, especially the risotto. The dish came last after we already finished everything else. They turn off all the lights and do this firing of the wok thing for a birthday too in case you want to come here for your birthday.<//Text>

<Time>1410284930767< /Time><Rate>5</Rate><Text>One of my favorite restaurants in the LA area. LOOOVE Musha!

The menu can seem daunting to those unfamiliar with Japanese tapas, but the staff is very friendly and full of recommendations. Here are my list of absolutely must tries:

- the cheese risotto, which is scooped out of a $400 chunk of parmigiano reggiano.
- french baguette stuffed with scallops and cheese
- beef tongue, lightly grilled and then sprinkled with salt and lemon juice

Dishes such as the ebi mayo mayo (much like the Chinese dish walnut shrimp), pork belly and the grilled chicken leg are also fantastic but not as imperative. I've tried mostly everything on the menu and so far nothing has been even slightly disappointing. It's roughly $5-7 a dish, so dinners come to about $20-30 a person.

Like most izakayas, the place is small and cozy, so make a reservation if you're planning on going during the weekend!< /Text>< Pics>

I really like the staff at 7 Day Dental.  But the service is not always so good.  Hence the 2 stars.  I think they are good for regular check-ups and cleanings. But anything beyond that, not so much.  The following is my experience.

I came in to repair a tooth that came loose from my upper denture.  The dentist fixed the problem but also recommended I take care of removing the remaining loose teeth that I had.  I agreed and set-up an appointment for the extractions.  The following is a list of the things that surprised and disappointed me from the experience and subsequent follow-ups.

1.	 The extraction dentist had me remove the upper denture, wrapped it in a paper towel and had me hold it.  This is very minor.  But it did strike me as unprofessional.  Every other dentist I‚Äôve been to have cleaned my denture and left it on a tray until the visit was finished.
2.	The dentist was originally going to let me go toothless for 4-6 weeks while my gums heeled from the extractions.  I was super surprised.  I had to ask for a temporary.  It seems like this should have been offered and not requested.
3.	I had to remind the dentist extracting the teeth to take an impression for the temporary denture before removing my remaining teeth.  He protested and said he would do it after the extractions since he had already started numbing my gums.  I questioned him asking if he was sure that would be ok since my gums would be sensitive after the extractions.  I asked that he please talk with the original dentist I spoke to before proceeding.  The dentist stopped him and corrected him, stating that the impressions needed to be taken first.  It was as if they had not consulted with each other on what was to be done.  I would have expected if they had not had a chance to speak, then at a minimum a note would have been left in my file with instructions.
4.	I returned in a few days to get the temporary and was surprised at how off it was from the previous partial denture that was removed.  But then I realized because the dentist did not provide an impression of both the top denture with a mold of the bottom teeth to the lab, they had no reference to match it to.  I didn‚Äôt think anything of it at the time the impression was taken.  But when I saw how off the temporary was, then I realized why previous dentists I went to took impressions of both the top and bottom, and sent both to the lab.
5.	Six weeks later now that my mouth has healed I returned for the permanent denture impressions.  I was disappointed to find out that protruding bone should have been filed down during the extractions so that the dentures could fit smoothly.  I was informed that I would have to wait 2 weeks to get approval for the procedure and then wait another 4-6 weeks for my mouth to heal before taking impressions for the dentures.  WHAT!!!!! I couldn‚Äôt believe it. Why was this not determined during my original visits??
6.	And today I called to confirm that the request for the latest procedure has been approved.  And was informed that it does not appear that the request was ever submitted.  But they will put in in today.  At this point I am just tired.
